# Imperative 1: Building Supply Chain Resilience in Consumer Goods {#imperative-1:-building-supply-chain-resilience-in-consumer-goods}

## Executive Summary {#executive-summary}

The $8.6 trillion consumer goods industry stands at a crossroads. Unprecedented disruptions have exposed fundamental vulnerabilities in traditional supply chain approaches, with organizations losing 6-10% of annual revenue to supply chain failures. This report outlines why supply chain transformation has become a board-level priority, the compelling urgency for immediate action, and how Databricks enables the intelligence-driven supply network that modern market conditions demand.

### Why Change? Why Consumer Goods Supply Chains Must Transform

Today's consumer goods leaders face a stark reality: the supply chain models that served them for decades have become significant liabilities. Global networks optimized for efficiency now represent critical points of failure in an increasingly volatile world.

Consider the evidence: Empty store shelves. Missed revenue opportunities. Escalating inventory costs. Brand damage from product recalls. These aren't isolated incidents but symptoms of systemic vulnerability. McKinsey research shows disruptions have led to losses exceeding 45% of a year's EBITDA for affected companies, while stockouts alone drive $1.5 trillion in lost sales annually.

Traditional approaches fail because they were never designed for today's challenges:

* Complex global sourcing networks create blind spots in supplier assessment, with 65% of supply chain failures traced to lower-tier suppliers according to Deloitte research. Modern organizations require visibility into tier-2 and tier-3 suppliers, but 45% of companies operate with limited upstream visibility.  
* Fragmented data ecosystems undermine decision-making, with critical information trapped in legacy systems. The typical consumer goods manufacturer manages 50+ discrete data streams — from social media sentiment to IoT sensors — but lacks the capabilities to integrate these signals for actionable intelligence.  
* Outdated collaboration protocols create costly friction between trading partners. A staggering 68% of retail-supplier data exchanges still rely on SFTP despite its complete lack of real-time capabilities, with manual integrations consuming 500+ hours annually per enterprise relationship.

The limitations of legacy approaches create a clear mandate for transformation. As McKinsey notes, "AI-powered supply chains aren't the future—they're the price of admission."

### Why Now? The Urgency: Why Consumer Goods Companies Must Act Now

The imperative for supply chain transformation isn't simply about improvement — it's about survival. Consumer goods companies face a perfect storm of pressures that make immediate action essential:

Accelerating disruption frequency threatens continuous operations. The number of global supply chain disruptions reached 11,642 in 2021, with 79% of companies experiencing significant impacts. Organizations lacking modern resilience capabilities experience 42% longer recovery times from these events.

Regulatory requirements demand comprehensive supply visibility. The FDA's Rule 204 requires complete traceability data within 24 hours during investigations, while evolving greenhouse gas emissions regulations demand tracking of Scope 3 supply chain emissions. Non-compliance risks substantial penalties.

Inflationary pressures squeeze margins as input costs rise. Amid 9.1% input cost inflation, 58% of CPG manufacturers now require real-time retailer demand data to optimize production. Those relying on outdated demand signals face margin erosion and missed growth opportunities.

Digital-native competitors leverage modern capabilities to gain market share. Companies using AI-driven forecasting achieve 30-50% higher accuracy than conventional approaches, directly translating to lower safety stock requirements, reduced waste, and optimized replenishment cycles.

The financial stakes couldn't be higher. Supply chain disruptions now cost organizations 6-10% of annual revenues, while stockouts contribute to $1.1 trillion in lost sales annually. Companies without multi-tier mapping experience 3.4x more stockouts during crises, with average incident costs exceeding $1.1 million per occurrence.

Leading organizations recognize that waiting is no longer an option. As Deloitte's research reveals, 79% of companies with mature supply chain capabilities outperform peers in revenue growth, while those lacking robust capabilities face existential risk.

### Why Databricks: Enabling the Intelligence-Driven Supply Network

The Databricks Data Intelligence Platform delivers the unified analytics, real-time processing, and collaborative framework needed to transform supply chain operations from reactive cost centers to proactive value drivers. Six core capabilities distinguish Databricks as the optimal foundation for supply chain transformation:

1. **Real-Time Intelligence at Scale**: Databricks delivers sub-second latency for real-time streaming workloads, enabling immediate response to emerging disruptions. This real-time architecture reduces time-to-insight by 60%, identifying supplier risks within 47 minutes versus 14-day industry standards. The platform processes 3.8 petabytes of data daily across 22 data types while providing petabyte-scale AI model training capabilities. This speed extends to analytics, where companies are no longer constrained by scaling capacity to run large predictive models. Companies are achieving up to 30% greater forecast accuracy compared to older methods, and simulating 250,000+ disruption scenarios hourly providing unprecedented visibility into potential supply chain risks  
2. **Enterprise-Grade Data Governance**: Unity Catalog provides centralized access control, column-level lineage, and audit logging across all data assets, ensuring regulatory compliance while enabling secure collaboration. This governance framework automates FDA Rule 204 compliance, tracing food safety data from raw materials to retail shelves in under 24 hours.  
3. **End-to-End Integrated AI Suite**: Mosaic AI, built on Databricks’ Data Intelligence Platform, empowers Consumer Goods companies to develop custom AI models—including cutting-edge generative AI and large language models—tailored to their specific needs. By integrating data management, AI model development, and deployment in one unified environment, Mosaic AI streamlines operations, reduces costs, and accelerates ROI. From supply chain optimization and process automation to real-time analytics, Mosaic AI addresses critical manufacturing challenges and scales effortlessly as data grows.   
4. **Seamless Real-time Data Sharing**: Delta Sharing enables secure, real-time data exchange with suppliers and retailers without data duplication or ETL. This zero-copy architecture reduces cloud storage costs by 30% and slashes supplier onboarding from 14 weeks to 9 days.  
5. **Strategic Partnerships that Simplify Integration**. Exclusive partnerships with SAP, along with relevant partnerships including Palantir, Aveva, Salesforce and data sharing access with Walmart, Circana and more, allow IT organizations to focus on solving business problems, while eliminating custom ETL.

### Measurable Business Impact

Consumer goods companies implementing the Databricks Data Intelligence Platform achieve transformative outcomes across key financial metrics:

Revenue Protection and Growth:

* 18% reduction in stockouts through AI-optimized inventory  
* 5% revenue growth through enhanced supplier collaboration  
* 19% sales lift from targeted digital campaigns versus 9% from traditional channels

Cost Optimization:

* 20-30% reduction in carrying costs through AI-driven inventory optimization  
* 42% improvement in logistics costs through ML-optimized routing  
* 17% lower TCO through zero-copy data sharing

Risk Mitigation:

* 40% fewer supply chain disruptions via AI-driven risk prediction  
* 65% faster risk response times using real-time alerts  
* 34% reduction in third-party risk exposure

Operational Excellence:

* 30-50% higher forecast accuracy through multi-variable modeling  
* 35% improvement in inventory turnover via predictive demand sensing  
* 72-hour category review cycles versus six weeks with manual methods

## Detail: Supply Chain Resiliency for Consumer Goods: A Strategic Imperative for the Digital Age {#detail:-supply-chain-resiliency-for-consumer-goods:-a-strategic-imperative-for-the-digital-age}

Imagine you’re steering a massive ship through unpredictable seas—one day the waters are calm, the next a sudden storm forces an emergency course correction. That’s the reality faced by today’s consumer goods companies navigating global supply chains. Traditionally, many businesses plotted their course using historical data and manual processes. But as recent years have shown—from unexpected geopolitical tensions to climate emergencies—this kind of slow, reactive strategy is no longer sufficient.

Today’s supply chain disruptions can wipe out up to 10% of a company’s annual revenue, and sometimes far more, when you account for longer-term brand damage and missed opportunities. Meanwhile, leaders in the field—such as McKinsey, Deloitte, and Accenture—estimate that those same disruptions also represent a **trillion-dollar opportunity** for businesses that can adapt quickly and smartly. It’s a profound paradox: the same forces that threaten margins and market share can also be harnessed to unlock massive growth if companies modernize their approach.

Below, we’ll explore the **core reasons** consumer goods organizations must change now, the **urgency** behind that change, and how **Databricks** provides the data-driven engine these companies need to become truly resilient.

### The Mounting Need for Change

Picture a global network of interconnected suppliers: a packaging materials provider in Southeast Asia, a chemical producer in Eastern Europe, multiple distribution centers across North America, and dozens more. A political crisis breaks out, or a supply partner is suddenly embroiled in a quality scandal. Within hours, production halts. Customers get frustrated by empty shelves. Social media lights up. Shareholders demand answers.

In the consumer goods space—worth well over **USD 8 trillion**—traditional supply chain strategies rely on past trends and best guesses. But new research reveals the high cost of continuing this way:

* **Financial Impact**: Disruptions can force an organization to lose 6–10% of yearly revenue.  
* **Brand Risk**: When consumers discover lapses in ethical sourcing, a company’s brand perception can erode by 9–14%.  
* **Complexity Overload**: Tier-2 and tier-3 supplier risk, climate regulations, and rapidly changing consumer preferences complicate forecasting and planning.

Leaders in every functional area—finance, operations, technology, and beyond—feel the pressure. According to Deloitte, **79% of companies with mature supply chain capabilities** outperform peers in revenue growth. In other words, the cost of not modernizing is extremely high, and the rewards for improving are just as significant.

### Why Now? A Sense of Urgency

You might be thinking, “Haven’t these issues always been around? Why the rush?” The truth is, **all the warning lights are flashing red at once**:

1. **Unpredictable Events**: Geopolitical tensions and severe weather events are happening more frequently, making routine operations risky if you lack real-time insights.  
2. **Customer Expectations**: With e-commerce and next-day delivery as the norm, any delay or out-of-stock situation means lost sales and potentially lost loyalty.  
3. **Regulatory Pressures**: Laws like GDPR in Europe and the California Delete Act in the U.S. require transparent, auditable supply chain data—something legacy systems can’t always provide.  
4. **Sustainability Demands**: Consumers increasingly prefer brands with ethical sourcing and lower carbon footprints, pressuring companies to trace supply chains more rigorously.

These challenges aren’t just on the horizon—they’re here. A single disruption can cost millions in lost sales and tarnish brand equity overnight. Many leaders worry that delaying digital transformation will mean falling behind competitors who already leverage real-time data and analytics.

## Three Critical Pillars of Supply Chain Resiliency {#three-critical-pillars-of-supply-chain-resiliency}

Databricks thinks about building supply chain resiliency in three areas:

* **Reduce external risk with suppliers**.  
* **Improve the prediction and management of inventory**.   
* **Drive greater execution through easier collaboration between suppliers and retailers**. 

### [Supplier Risk Management](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1AD4S6QRhr3UCN_Zoo5FVnXyJrTI4MaTmJua4bMkNjH4/edit?usp=sharing)

Think of supplier risk management as an early warning radar. Instead of finding out too late that a critical supplier is about to go bankrupt or is unreachable because of a natural disaster, real-time risk management can flag danger immediately. This helps companies identify problems with the supply of materials with enough time to make adjustments such as purchasing supply from alternative sources without paying higher rates or expedited shipping.

#### **Why Change?**

* **Delayed Reactions Are Costly**: Companies without multi-tier visibility can take weeks to respond to disruptions. By that time, the damage is done—empty shelves, unhappy retailers, and rattled investors.  
* **Blind Spots**: Lower-tier suppliers often operate in regions with higher geopolitical or climatic risks. Traditional quarterly assessments miss these real-time threats.  
* **Impact on Brand**: A single product recall can permanently alienate consumers, especially if they learn it was preventable through more diligent oversight.

#### **Why Now?**

* **Growing Complexity**: As global sourcing webs expand, it only takes one disrupted link to fracture the entire chain.  
* **Geopolitical and environmental disruptions**. Tariffs, epidemics, civil strife, and disruptions from weather, drought, and other factors are increasingly disrupting supply chains. Companies need to be able to quickly monitor risks and determine how to react.

#### **How Databricks is Differentiated**

* **Real-Time Alerts**: By integrating diverse data sources—from internal ERPs, like supplier documents, satellite imagery, social media chatter—Databricks enables companies to flag disruptive signals within minutes.  
* **Predictive Modeling**: AI can spot early signs of financial instability or compliance violations, letting you switch suppliers or reroute shipments before disaster strikes.  
* **Scenario Testing**: With the platform’s advanced analytics, you can simulate thousands of “what if” scenarios—natural disasters, global conflict, regulatory changes—and develop contingency plans on the fly.

### Inventory & Demand Management

Suffering from stockouts is more than just losing immediate revenue; it can undermine trust if customers repeatedly encounter empty shelves. On the flip side, overstocking drives waste and eats into margins. Striking the perfect balance requires technology that can handle a flood of data from every direction.

Why Change?

* **Multiple Data Streams**: Consumer trends can pivot overnight, influenced by social media or a high-profile influencer. Traditional forecasting models can’t keep up with that level of volatility.  
  * **Complex Inputs**: Sales data, weather patterns, economic indicators, and even competitor promotions can all shift demand.

Why Now?

* **Cost of Inaccuracy**: McKinsey estimates **USD 1 trillion** lost annually to stockouts. Meanwhile, overproduction leads to markdowns and supply chain bloat.  
  * **AI is Table Stakes**: Leading firms are using AI to drive forecast accuracy rates significantly higher than human planners can achieve on their own.

How Databricks is Differentiated

* **End-to-End Data Integration**: Easily merge structured (e.g., ERP) and unstructured (e.g., social media) data sources in a single environment.  
  * **AI-Powered Forecasting**: Automation and machine learning deliver real-time forecast updates that reflect the latest market signals.  
  * **Digital Twin Simulations**: Test countless permutations of pricing and promotional strategies virtually before committing resources, reducing guesswork and wasted spending.

### Retailer Collaboration

In a competitive consumer marketplace, seamless collaboration between manufacturers and retailers can give both parties a significant edge. Yet many still rely on clunky, decades-old methods of exchanging data—like SFTP transfers—that are neither timely nor secure.

Why Change?

* **Legacy Data Systems**: Slow data transfers and labor-intensive reconciliation processes lead to delays, errors, and ultimately, lost sales.  
  * **Scalability Issues**: Onboarding a new retail partner can take months with traditional systems, killing momentum for new product launches or seasonal promotions.

Why Now?

* **Market Speed**: Retailers expect near-real-time inventory visibility and shared insights to ensure shelves stay stocked. Any friction in collaboration hurts both sides.  
  * **Regulatory Compliance**: Modern data-sharing solutions are required to meet increasingly strict privacy and compliance standards.

How Databricks is Differentiated

* **Open and Secure Data Sharing**: Delta Sharing provides a cloud-neutral, zero-copy way to let partners view live data, eliminating outdated file exchange.  
  * **Real-Time Visibility**: Both manufacturers and retailers can instantly see inventory positions, sales performance, and promotional results—unlocking more accurate production, distribution, and pricing decisions.  
  * **Governance Built-In**: Automated lineage and governance controls simplify compliance, preventing unauthorized access or data misuse.

### Why Databricks Is the Key Enabler

It’s not enough to know you need a digital overhaul; you also need the right technology platform to get there. That’s where Databricks stands out. Unlike patchwork solutions that require multiple vendors and endless custom integrations, Databricks offers a unified data and AI platform designed for speed, security, and scalability.

The Databricks Data Intelligence Platform delivers the unified analytics, real-time processing, and collaborative framework needed to transform supply chain operations from reactive cost centers to proactive value drivers. Six core capabilities distinguish Databricks as the optimal foundation for supply chain transformation:

1. Real-Time Intelligence at Scale: Databricks delivers sub-second latency for real-time streaming workloads, enabling immediate response to emerging disruptions. This real-time architecture reduces time-to-insight by 60%, identifying supplier risks within 47 minutes versus 14-day industry standards.  
2. Unified Multi-Modal Analytics: By processing structured, semi-structured, and unstructured data in a single platform, Databricks enables comprehensive analysis of satellite imagery, IoT sensor data, and unstructured supplier documents alongside traditional ERP data. This unified approach yields 92% accuracy in predicting market disruptions.  
3. Enterprise-Grade Governance: Unity Catalog provides centralized access control, column-level lineage, and audit logging across all data assets, ensuring regulatory compliance while enabling secure collaboration. This governance framework automates FDA Rule 204 compliance, tracing food safety data from raw materials to retail shelves in under 24 hours.  
4. AI-Powered Decision Intelligence: Mosaic AI enables consumer goods companies to harness the power of both traditional ML and generative AI for supply chain optimization. For demand forecasting, it achieves 30% higher accuracy compared to manual methods, while reducing LLM costs by 80% for unstructured data analysis.  
5. Seamless Partner Collaboration: Delta Sharing enables secure, real-time data exchange with suppliers and retailers without data duplication or ETL. This zero-copy architecture reduces cloud storage costs by 30% and slashes supplier onboarding from 14 weeks to 9 days.  
6. Proven Enterprise Scale: The platform processes 3.8 petabytes of data daily across 22 data types while providing petabyte-scale AI model training capabilities. This performance enables simulation of 250,000+ disruption scenarios hourly, providing unprecedented visibility into potential supply chain risks.

Databricks Data Intelligence Platform is a holistic capability that simplifies the Supply Chain technology ecosystem by centralizing data in one location and making it immediately available for use.

# Imperative 2: Transforming Brand, Consumer and Retail Insights {#imperative-2:-transforming-brand,-consumer-and-retail-insights}

## Executive Summary {#executive-summary-1}

**Why Change?** Consumer Goods firms face critical challenges in their current approach to consumer and brand insights:

* **High Cost and Low Value**: Dependence on costly third-party data providers (NielsenIQ, Mintel, Kantar) delivers incomplete, delayed, and overly aggregated insights.  
* **Limited Granularity and Timeliness**: Legacy methods obscure valuable details needed for agile decision-making, causing delayed reactions to market shifts and missed opportunities for product innovation and precise marketing attribution.  
* **Consumer Data Marginalization**: Data remains siloed and tactical, weakening cross-functional collaboration and leaving CPGs disconnected from direct consumer relationships. This reduces their responsiveness and efficiency, undermining competitive advantage.

**Why Invest Now?** Immediate investment in advanced consumer data and AI capabilities is strategically critical due to:

* **Pressures for Profitable Growth**: With traditional pricing strategies exhausted and wealth increasingly concentrated among top earners, deeper consumer understanding is essential for profitable volume growth.  
* **Regulatory Shifts and Privacy Constraints**: The demise of third-party cookies and stricter privacy regulations (GDPR, CCPA) increase the value and necessity of first-party and zero-party data.  
* **Rise of Retail Media Networks (RMNs)**: Brands must leverage RMNs effectively, requiring sophisticated data analytics to target ads, measure incrementality, and maximize ROI from retailer collaboration.  
* **Emergence of New Data Sources**: Technologies like synthetic data, web scraping, NLP, and image analytics offer unprecedented opportunities for granular, real-time consumer insights.

**The Envisioned Solution** A modernized approach positions consumer data as a strategic, integrated asset across all business functions:

* **Centralized Consumer Data Hub**: Integrating traditional, emerging, and unstructured data sources to deliver timely, granular insights.  
* **Advanced AI-driven Analytics**: Real-time mining of consumer sentiment, trend detection, and competitive dynamics through NLP, computer vision, and generative AI.  
* **Enhanced Data Governance and Collaboration**: Ensuring regulatory compliance, enabling seamless data sharing internally and externally via tools like Unity Catalog and Delta Sharing.  
* **Self-service and Democratized Insights**: Empowering business users with intuitive platforms (e.g., Databricks Genie) for agile decision-making across marketing, innovation, category management, and supply chain operations.

**Why Databricks?** Databricks' Lakehouse architecture uniquely addresses CPG industry needs by offering:

* Unified real-time processing and simplified data infrastructure.  
* Robust governance for regulatory compliance.  
* Open, seamless data sharing for collaboration.  
* Integrated AI and ML capabilities enhancing analytics depth and speed.  
* Accessible, user-friendly platforms promoting business agility and responsiveness.

**Key Strategic Benefits**

* **Immediate ROI through precise marketing attribution and optimized promotional spend.**  
* **Long-term competitive advantage from deeper consumer relationships and insights.**  
* **Enhanced agility enabling proactive response to rapidly changing consumer behaviors.**

Investing now positions Consumer Goods firms to thrive amidst intensifying competitive pressures, evolving regulatory landscapes, and rapidly shifting consumer expectations.

## Why Change {#why-change}

There are three fundamental shifts that are occurring in Consumer Goods today that involve consumer and brand insights.

**1\) A High dependence on costly third-party data and analysis (NielsenIQ, Mintel,Kantar, media agencies etc.):** Spending on third-party data and analysis services is the single largest source of analytic spending in any consumer goods company, often vastly outweighing internal technology spend. For decades, consumer goods firms have relied on syndicated retail scanner data and consumer panels for market insights. Services from NielsenIQ, IRI, Kantar and others provide sales volumes, market share, and panel survey data – but **at a steep price and with limitations**. Vendor pricing ranges widely: companies pay *“from thousands for a single report to millions for ongoing data and software”* in annual fees ([Syndicated store data for retail | Observa](https://www.observanow.com/syndicated-store-data-for-retail/#:~:text=There%20are%20ways%20to%20obtain,for%20ongoing%20data%20and%20software)). Even with such investment, coverage is incomplete: *“syndicated vendors don’t provide data for all retailers or all products”* ([Syndicated store data for retail | Observa](https://www.observanow.com/syndicated-store-data-for-retail/#:~:text=When%20it%20comes%20to%20accuracy%2C,garden%20categories%20in%20mass%20merchandisers)). (For instance, some major retailers like Whole Foods historically refused to share data, leaving blind spots ([Syndicated store data for retail | Observa](https://www.observanow.com/syndicated-store-data-for-retail/#:~:text=When%20it%20comes%20to%20accuracy%2C,garden%20categories%20in%20mass%20merchandisers)).) The data often lacks granularity (e.g. aggregated to weekly or regional levels) and is delayed. Traditional retail sales reports might arrive weeks after transactions, far too slow for agile decision-making in today’s market. In short, CPGs are **paying more and more for data that is less and less sufficient**.

**2\) Legacy approaches to consumer and brand insights suffer from critical shortcomings in timeliness and granularity**. 

Typically delivered at infrequent intervals—monthly or quarterly—and presented at aggregate levels, these insights are often limited to a small percentage of groups within a consumer goods company.

Aggregation obscures crucial details: when a product underperforms, traditional syndicated data (e.g., Nielsen or IRI) indicates that a decline occurred but rarely clarifies why—was it due to regional factors, specific consumer segments, or issues like packaging identified through customer reviews? Consequently, important signals such as emerging niche trends, shifts in consumer sentiment, or local preferences often remain unnoticed. Retailers benefit from detailed, transaction-level data, whereas manufacturers receive generalized snapshots that limit their ability to respond effectively. Indeed, industry analysts emphasize that third-party data is frequently "not always as relevant, complete or timely as first-hand data."

These limitations leave critical business questions unanswered and reinforce a dependency on pricing and promotion to move product, which erodes margins. Brands struggle to gain a real-time understanding of consumer affinities, brand sentiment or immediate campaign effectiveness. Consumer insights teams often rely on outdated, potentially biased methods like surveys and focus groups, while retailer-provided sales data lacks context around broader consumer behavior. The imprecision of data imposes a particular challenge with marketing attribution, with CPG marketers frequently unable to pinpoint precisely why consumers are making which decisions in what channels, due largely to an absence of first-party data. This gap prevents informed optimization of marketing spend.

New product development decisions similarly suffer. Launch performance typically surfaces in syndicated data months later, delaying essential corrective actions. Ultimately, these gaps result in costly mistakes and missed opportunities: ineffective promotions, unaddressed negative consumer sentiment, and delayed recognition of category shifts that competitors capitalize on first.

3\) **Consumer Goods firms do not consider consumer data as a first class domain. Consumer is a marketing tactic, not an operational source**. Consumer insights has historically been used to derive initial insights to target brand messaging, target consumers for advertising, or explain sales to key demographics. In these uses, consumer data remains in data silos and is used tactically. 

Consumer data is not a first class citizen for most Consumer Goods firms. As noted, most consumer goods firms have scant first-party data because the retailer “owns” the consumer relationship. Unlike a DTC brand that knows every customer’s identity and purchase history, a toothpaste or snack manufacturer sees mostly anonymized, aggregated data. This puts CPGs at arm’s length from the very consumers they serve. 

Externally, **manufacturers and retailers historically share limited data**. Trust and alignment issues, along with technical barriers, mean collaborative data exchange is minimal. (CPGs sometimes get category summaries from retailers, but rarely the granular shopper-level data due to privacy and competitive concerns.)

Because data is siloed, cross-functional collaboration suffers. Insights that require input from multiple sources (e.g. combining social media sentiment with sales figures and inventory levels) are hard to produce. Different departments might use different tools and metrics, leading to inconsistent “truths.” Additionally, CPG companies working with retail partners often lack a seamless way to collaborate on shared data (e.g. joint business planning metrics) – data lives in PDFs or spreadsheets emailed back and forth, rather than a real-time shared view.

The consequence of these challenges is that **CPG companies today often make critical decisions with suboptimal insight**. They may over-spend on trade promotions that don’t work (because they can’t pinpoint which promotions truly drove sales). They may miss early signs of a trend – for instance, a niche competitor gaining cult status via TikTok – until it’s too late to respond. They may continue producing a product in excess because supply chain forecasts weren’t updated with the latest demand signals, leading to markdowns or write-offs. In marketing, lack of feedback loops means brands can’t adapt messaging in real-time, resulting in wasted media dollars. Overall, the organization becomes **slower and less targeted**, a serious liability when new agile D2C brands and retail giants are exploiting data expertly. As Bain noted, many large CPGs are *“ill-adapted to the new normal”* and need to *“rewrite their growth playbooks”* with technology at the core ([Consumer Products Report 2025: CPG Industry Outlook | Bain & Company](https://www.bain.com/insights/consumer-products-report-2025-reclaiming-relevance-in-the-gen-ai-era/#:~:text=economic%20hardship%2C%20fragmenting%20needs%2C%20and,loss%20jabs)) ([Consumer Products Report 2025: CPG Industry Outlook | Bain & Company](https://www.bain.com/insights/consumer-products-report-2025-reclaiming-relevance-in-the-gen-ai-era/#:~:text=For%20consumer%20packaged%20goods%20companies%2C,offers%20renewed%20hope%20of%20reinvention)).

In summary, the status quo of insight generation in consumer goods – characterized by expensive, lagged, and low-granularity data – is no longer tenable. Continuing this way means **flying blind in a storm**: consumer behaviors are changing faster than companies can detect, and traditional methods cannot keep up. The cost structure is upside-down (paying more for third-party data yet getting less value) and the internal friction to make sense of data is high. This is eroding competitive position: as some players move to modern, data-driven models, others who don’t change will fall behind.

**The imperative for change** is clear: consumer goods firms must overhaul their data and insight capabilities to gain a timely, granular, 360° understanding of their consumers, brands, and retail channels. Only then can they make proactive decisions – adjusting marketing on the fly, innovating products to precisely meet emerging needs, and optimizing retail execution store by store. The following sections delve into why this transformation must happen now, and how leveraging new data sources and AI technologies can close these insight gaps.

## Why Invest Now {#why-invest-now}

Consumer Goods firms **face significant financial headwinds** that require them to rethink their go-to-market approach, but **recent innovations in technology** make developing Consumer and Brand Insights more accessible than ever before. The call to action is not just to change eventually, but to invest **now**. Several converging factors make immediate investment in enhanced data and AI capabilities both strategically critical and time-sensitive:

**1\) Consumer Goods firms need to find new sources of profitable volume growth, and that begins with better insights.** Consumer Goods companies have been overly dependent on pricing as a strategy for driving revenue growth and are increasingly exposed. **All 50 of the top 50 largest publicly traded consumer goods companies owe a majority of their revenue growth over the past 5 years to price increases.** Meanwhile, consumers are tapped out. While the top quartile of earners has seen net wealth increase, the majority of consumers have seen net wealth stagnate or even decline. 

* **Top 10% of Earners.** Households in the top 10% (earning $250,000 or more annually) have experienced substantial growth in wealth, driven by increases in stock market values and real estate. Their consumer spending increased by 58% over four years (2019–2024), far outpacing inflation, which rose 21% during the same period.  
* **Middle Class.** The middle-class households (earning approximately $58,000–$96,000 annually) owned about 8% of total U.S. household wealth as of Q3 2024\. This equates to an average net worth of $480,000 per household. While middle-class wealth grew steadily until 2022, it has since declined slightly due to rising costs and limited liquidity in their assets (e.g., home equity and retirement accounts).  
* **Bottom 50%.** The bottom half of earners hold just 6% of total U.S. wealth, with much of their gains tied to illiquid assets like home values. Excluding Social Security benefits, their share drops to only 3%. Rising expenses and stagnant wages have limited wealth accumulation for this group, leaving them more vulnerable to economic shocks.

This leaves brands increasingly dependent on a small subset of the population for driving profitable revenue growth. Wealth inequality has reached record levels, with the top 10% increasingly driving economic growth and consumer spending. In contrast, lower-income households have seen limited gains and may opt-out of buying brands altogether. 

Consumer Goods firms most orient around the consumer to drive all aspects of their business, from new product development, brand positioning, media but also sales strategies, supply chain planning, category leadership and more.

In a mature industry increasingly dependent on market share to drive growth, a 2024 survey of CPG executives showed a *24 percentage point surge* [in the share who are prioritizing AI and new data capabilities](https://www.bain.com/insights/consumer-products-report-2025-reclaiming-relevance-in-the-gen-ai-era/#:~:text=Scale%20to%20accelerate,suite%20preoccupation). In the same survey, fully 90% of CPG execs said their organization is thinking about AI use cases – yet only 6% have a clear plan to generate business value from it. 

2\) **Regulatory and privacy shifts (the end of easy data) are making consumer data more valuable:** The external environment for data is changing with regulations like GDPR, CCPA, and the deprecation of third-party cookies. Come 2024/2025, targeting consumers via third-party data (cookies, device IDs) is much harder. Google’s phase-out of cookies in Chrome, for example, means brands can no longer rely on third-party tracking to understand consumer behavior on the web. This makes **first-party and zero-party data** strategies essential. 

Retailers have a trove of *first-party data* (transaction histories, loyalty data), which is one reason retail media networks are surging (more on that below). Consumer goods companies need to build their own direct data pipelines (through D2C initiatives, loyalty programs, etc.) or risk being **blinded by privacy rules**. 

3\) **New data sources are emerging**. *Zero-party data*, which is voluntarily given by consumers (e.g. preferences they input, survey responses), is emerging as a key asset because it’s privacy-compliant and explicit. A recent EY analysis calls zero-party data *“the next frontier in consumer strategy,”* noting it is a **mutually beneficial exchange** – customers willingly share data in return for value (personalized offers, loyalty points), and companies get [high-quality info](https://www.ey.com/en_us/insights/consulting/zero-party-data-is-the-next-frontier-in-consumer-strategy#:~:text=match%20at%20L481%20,incentives%20for%20submitting%20their%20data) with privacy consent. 

**Companies that invest now in zero-party data collection will have an advantage as third-party avenues shrink**. Meanwhile, regulations also hamper third-party sharing: as noted earlier, [stricter rules have *“scuppered CPG brands’*](https://goamplifi.com/eu/knowledge-base/cpg-the-impact-of-first-party-data-deficit-blog#:~:text=wholesalers%2C%20CPG%20brands%20haven%E2%80%99t%20benefitted,themselves%20and%20their%20end%20customers) *access to the customer data they need”* from partners. 

Looking ahead, by 2025, Gartner [predicts **synthetic data**](https://replica-analytics.com/blog/new-gartner-survey-suggests-synthetic-data-is-the-future-of-data-sharing/#:~:text=New%20Gartner%20survey%20suggests%20synthetic,of%20privacy%20violation%20sanctions) (artificially generated data) will be widely used to avoid using personal consumer data – *“reducing personal customer data collection, avoiding 70% of privacy violation sanctions”*. By 2026, 75% of businesses are expected to use generative AI to create synthetic customer data. **This trend is twofold**: on one hand, real consumer data is harder to get (unless consumers give it to you directly); on the other, technologies exist to generate useful proxy data. Investing now positions a company to operate in this new paradigm – building trust with consumers for direct data, and using AI-driven methods like synthetic data to enrich models without violating privacy. Those who delay will find themselves stuck when the old sources dry up.

4\) **CPGs must understand consumers to tap into Retail Media Networks**. The past few years have seen retailers from Amazon and Walmart to Kroger and Sephora launch their own media platforms, allowing brands to buy ads targeting the retailer’s shoppers on their sites and beyond. **Retail Media Networks (RMNs)** are growing at breakneck speed.

The top 5 RMNs account for 87% of all retail media network spend, but the the greatest opportunity may exist in the remaining 13%. Faced with fewer participants, these RMNs present an efficiency arbitrage play for Consumer Goods firms if those firms can target the right consumers.

For CPG brands, this represents both an opportunity and a mandate. Opportunity, because they can leverage retailers’ first-party data to target ads at the point of purchase (e.g. advertise a snack to people who just put a soda in their online cart). Mandate, because retailers are increasingly **monetizing their data advantage**, and CPGs must participate to stay visible. In fact, retail media is *“[swallowing up shopper and trade marketing budgets](https://www.emarketer.com/content/2025-trend-retail-media-networks-unfamiliar-waters-satisfy-advertiser-demands-incrementality#:~:text=2025%20trend%3A%20Retail%20media%20networks,for%20RMN%20advertisers%2C%20but)”* that brands traditionally spent elsewhere. 

The implication is that to get ROI on these spends, CPG companies need advanced data analytics. For example, **measuring performance across different retail media platforms requires unifying data from each retailer’s reports and one’s own sales – a complex task without a strong data platform**. 

The rise of RMNs is part of a broader shift: *retailers themselves are becoming data/insight companies*. They have **“a goldmine of proprietary customer data”** from online shopping and loyalty programs. They use it to attract brand advertising and to negotiate for trade dollars. **Consumer goods firms need to counterbalance this by developing their own robust insight generation** – both to make the most of retailer data, and to be less reliant on what retailers choose to share. Brands investing in AI can ensure their retail media spend truly drives incremental sales (for instance by analyzing *incrementality* of campaigns – the top [KPI for retail media](https://www.emarketer.com/content/2025-trend-retail-media-networks-unfamiliar-waters-satisfy-advertiser-demands-incrementality#:~:text=2025%20trend%3A%20Retail%20media%20networks,for%20RMN%20advertisers%2C%20but). Those who don’t may see their margins erode as they pour money in without understanding the returns.

5\) **New data availability and techniques to exploit it:** **Innovative data sources and AI techniques have emerged** that simply weren’t feasible a few years ago. This opens exciting avenues for those ready to invest:

* **Synthetic data***:* As mentioned, AI can now generate realistic datasets (customer profiles, transaction logs, etc.) that mirror real data without using actual personal info.   
* **Zero-party data***:* Savvy brands are launching **direct consumer engagement platforms** to solicit preferences. For example, beauty brands might ask users to take a quiz about skin type and product preferences (offering a coupon in return) – all that declared data (zero-party) becomes incredibly valuable for tailoring products and marketing. Investing in systems to capture and integrate such data (e.g. through websites, apps, IoT-connected products) will yield a trove of proprietary insight others don’t have. Importantly, zero-party data is *highly accurate by definition* ([it’s literally what customers say they want](https://www.ey.com/en_us/insights/consulting/zero-party-data-is-the-next-frontier-in-consumer-strategy#:~:text=%2A%20Through%20the%20zero,incentives%20for%20submitting%20their%20data)).  
* **Web scraping and unstructured data mining***:* The internet is a rich source of consumer opinion and behavior data – if one can harness it. Today’s AI can parse **unstructured data** like social media posts, images, videos, product reviews, blog comments, etc., at scale to extract trends and sentiment. This is a game changer. Consider **images on social media**: Fashion and beauty brands now use image recognition AI to spot emerging styles.   
  * Trend forecasting agencies like Heuritech use AI to scan *“over three million social media images a day,”* helping [brands predict what consumers](https://www.wallpaper.com/fashion-beauty/is-ai-the-future-of-fashion-trend-forecasting#:~:text=Is%20AI%20the%20future%20of,fashion%20trend%20forecasting) will want to wear. That means a clothing company can detect, say, that crochet bags are spiking in Paris this week and adjust its merchandising or marketing accordingly in near real-time.  
  * Another example: consumer **product reviews** on e-commerce sites contain a wealth of feedback on product strengths and weaknesses. Not long ago it was infeasible to manually read thousands of reviews, but NLP (natural language processing) models now can **mine reviews for sentiment and specific product issues or feature requests**. One industry commentary noted that *“mining product reviews across multiple channels of consumer interaction is critical to gaining timely insights.”* ([Successful New Product Launch | Column | Consumer Goods Technology](https://consumergoods.com/successful-new-product-launch#:~:text=,store%20performance%20and%20planogram)) Leading companies are indeed doing this – for instance, beverage companies analyzing social media and review data to understand flavor trends and reactions. By investing in AI, CPGs can turn this unstructured data deluge into actionable insight (e.g. detect that a common complaint about a shampoo is its cap design, prompting a packaging change).  
* **Images and video analysis***:* Beyond social media photos for trends, image recognition can be applied in retail settings (checking shelf displays, tracking foot traffic via CCTV, etc.) and in product R\&D (analyzing how consumers use products through submitted photos/videos). Video analytics can glean insights such as how shoppers navigate aisles or how products are used in home environments, informing everything from planogram design to product instructions. Such data streams were largely untapped historically; AI makes them accessible now.  
* **Large language models (LLMs) and generative AI:** The generative AI wave has profound implications for insights. LLMs can summarize vast datasets, generate hypotheses, and even create content for testing. For example, a generative AI could draft a summary of “key reasons customers dislike Product X” by synthesizing thousands of reviews and social comments – work that would take human analysts weeks. It can also generate synthetic consumer opinions or creative concepts to test reactions. Crucially, LLMs allow **non-technical users to query data via natural language**, democratizing insights (more on this in the Databricks section with the Genie capability).

T**he data universe is expanding** and AI is the key to unlock it. The cost of sensors, storage, and compute has dropped such that collecting *and actually using* new data types is economically viable. Companies that invest now can leapfrog by feeding their decision-making with richer datasets (real-time weather, location data, social buzz, etc.). This yields a more holistic view of the consumer and the market.

In summary, **“Why invest now?”** – because the competitive clock is ticking, the external landscape demands it, new technologies make it rewarding, and leading companies have shown it works. The cost of waiting is a potential permanent setback: by the time a slow mover acts, the gap may be too wide to close. Conversely, investing now in data/AI-driven insights can deliver immediate wins (e.g. quick ROI projects in promotions or marketing) while building long-term capabilities that fortify the business. 

## The Envisioned Solution

**Consumer data must be elevated from a marketing tactic to a first-class data domain in CPG that helps firms differentiate in how they go to market across functions.**

We envision a solution that enables Consumer Goods firms:

1. Centralize their own Brand and Consumer data in one location.  
2. Tap into traditional data but also emerging and unstructured data that can be used to better understand emerging trends.  
3. Integrate these disparate sources to align with internal definitions and hierarchies  
4. Create analysis based on real-time insights, not weeks or months later.  
5. Enable companies to build their own insights and analytics internally, or securely expose data to partners to provide solutions.

This would accomplish this via:

* **Data partnerships**. Working with new data partners with access to web scraping, computer vision, IoT, social media and other data sets in addition to traditional data sources.  
* **Extracting relevant data from unstructured data**. Leveraging advanced AI-driven techniques, this solution rapidly mines consumer sentiment, identifies emerging trends, and monitors competitive dynamics in real-time. Natural Language Processing (NLP) and image/video analytics unlock valuable insights from vast, diverse datasets, enabling proactive decision-making across product development, marketing, and supply chain operations.  
* **Integrating disparate brand and consumer data to align with internal hierarchies and definitions using Workflows and Entity Resolution**.  
* **Protecting data**. Ensuring compliance with privacy regulations (GDPR, CCPA) and providing clear data lineage.   
* **Improving discovery and reuse of data across the entire company through Unity Catalog**.  
* **Enabling a rich ecosystem of internal and third-parties to work directly against this data via Delta Sharing**:  
  * Provide Enable third-party media agencies via Delta Sharing to build their own analysis.  
  * Identify and sign third-party ISVs who work in this space and have solutions that can reside on top of the data.  
  * Enable front line access to data accessible via self-service analysis and AI agents such as Genie, empower non-technical stakeholders to access real-time insights independently, significantly improving responsiveness and agility.   
  * Additionally, Databricks Apps facilitate rapid development of insights-driven applications tailored to specific business use cases, from retail execution to personalized marketing.

This solution is a composable architecture that centralizes data in the customer tenant, but allows them to attach partners on top of that data. By adopting this integrated Databricks solution, Consumer Goods firms can substantially reduce reliance on external analytics vendors, accelerate decision-making with granular, timely insights, and transform consumer data into a strategic asset, thus positioning themselves advantageously in a highly competitive market landscape.

## Why Databricks {#why-databricks}

Implementing a data and AI transformation requires the right technology platform. **Databricks** – with its Lakehouse architecture – has emerged as a leading choice for enterprises looking to unify data, analytics, and AI. For consumer goods firms aiming to boost brand, consumer, and retailer insights, Databricks offers distinct advantages. This section highlights *why Databricks* is the ideal platform:

| Capability Category | Databricks Advantage Relative to Google, Snowflake, Microsoft | Impact for Consumer Goods Firms |

| **Data Engineering & Real-time Processing** | Unified Lakehouse architecture provides native streaming & batch processing in one environment (vs. separate tools in Google BigQuery, Snowflake’s limited streaming, Azure’s fragmented services) | Rapid, simpler real-time insights for consumer behavior, quicker reaction to market shifts, reduced infrastructure complexity & cost |
| **Data Governance (Unity Catalog)** | Single, unified governance and discoverability solution across multiple clouds (vs. fragmented solutions in Google, Microsoft Purview complexity, limited lineage in Snowflake) | Enhanced regulatory compliance (GDPR, CCPA), simplified data discovery, democratized data access across departments (Marketing, Supply Chain, Category Management) |

| **Machine Learning** | Integrated MLflow and AutoML for seamless ML lifecycle management on a unified platform (vs. Google's separate Vertex AI, Snowflake’s minimal ML capabilities, Azure ML’s complexity) | Accelerated model deployment, streamlined consumer churn prediction, improved demand forecasting accuracy |

| **Strategic Partnerships (SAP, Circana, Walmart, Yobi)** | Exclusive, direct integrations and access to strategic datasets and platforms (vs. limited integration breadth in Snowflake, Google’s competitive barriers, Microsoft's narrower industry focus) | Unique competitive data advantages, reduced reliance on costly syndicated data, richer insights with exclusive access (Walmart Scintilla, SAP integrations), optimized category planning and execution |

Implementing a data and AI-driven insights platform like Databricks in a consumer goods organization will involve multiple decision-makers and stakeholders. Below is a table of **key buyer personas** at a typical CPG firm, including their titles, core responsibilities, pain points that this initiative addresses, and their strategic priorities (what they stand to gain):

| Role | Corporate Responsibilities | How This Addresses Their Need | Primary Metric for Evaluation |
| ----- | ----- | ----- | ----- |
| **Chief Marketing Officer (CMO)** | Brand positioning, consumer engagement, media spend effectiveness, driving profitable volume growth | Enables timely insights for targeted marketing, improved attribution of marketing spend, and precise consumer segmentation | Marketing ROI, Incremental Sales |
| **Chief Data & Analytics Officer (CDAO)** | Data strategy, data governance, analytics infrastructure, ensuring compliance with privacy regulations | Provides unified, compliant data management, reduces reliance on expensive third-party data, and democratizes data access across teams | Data Compliance, Cost Reduction, Data Accessibility |
| **Chief Information Officer (CIO)** | Technology infrastructure, IT cost management, supporting business agility through technology | Simplifies data infrastructure, reduces complexity, accelerates deployment of analytics applications and real-time data insights | IT Cost Reduction, Deployment Speed, Infrastructure Stability |
| **Head of Consumer Insights** | Consumer behavior analysis, consumer sentiment and trends monitoring, brand health assessment | Offers real-time granular consumer insights, emerging trend detection, and deeper brand analytics to support informed decision-making | Insight Accuracy, Speed of Insight Generation |
| **Head of Category Management** | Assortment planning, SKU rationalization, shelf execution, optimizing retail performance | Provides AI-driven insights into localized assortment, improved shelf compliance monitoring, and store execution performance | Assortment Optimization, Compliance Rates |
| **Chief Supply Chain Officer (CSCO)** | Supply chain planning, inventory optimization, demand forecasting accuracy | Integrates consumer sentiment and real-time demand signals into supply chain processes, enhancing forecasting accuracy and operational agility | Forecast Accuracy, Inventory Turns |
| **Head of Digital Marketing & Media** | Digital campaigns management, ad spend effectiveness, retail media network (RMN) performance evaluation | Delivers real-time analytics on digital campaign incrementality, RMN effectiveness, and dynamic content optimization | Campaign Incrementality, Return on Ad Spend (ROAS) |
| **Head of Product Innovation** | New product development, product feature optimization, response to consumer-driven trends | Provides direct consumer feedback, early trend detection, and rapid assessment of product performance post-launch | Product Success Rate, Speed to Market |
| **Head of Competitive Intelligence** | Competitor benchmarking, strategic positioning, market trend monitoring | Enables real-time competitor activity tracking and benchmarking, rapid identification of market shifts | Competitive Responsiveness, Benchmark Accuracy |

## **Data and AI Use Cases** {#data-and-ai-use-cases}

To concretize the impact of investing in data/AI capabilities, below is a table of **high-value use cases** for brand, consumer, and retailer insights in the consumer goods sector.

| Use Case Name | Description | Data Sources |
| ----- | ----- | ----- |
| **Real-Time Product Launch Tracker** | Immediate performance evaluation and feedback from multiple channels post-launch. | Social media sentiment, online reviews, sales data, zero-party surveys. |
| **Dynamic Pricing & Promotion Optimization** | Real-time, AI-driven promotional pricing optimization. | Transaction-level data, competitor pricing (web scraping), demand signals, RMN data. |
| **Micro-Trend Detection** | Identifying niche emerging consumer trends before they scale. | Social media images, video content, web scraping, sentiment analysis. |
| **Consumer Sentiment Heatmap** | Real-time geographical visualization of brand/product sentiment. | Social media geotags, NLP sentiment analysis, IoT foot traffic data. |
| **Campaign Incrementality Analysis** | Measuring real incremental sales driven by media spending. | RMN advertising data, POS data, first-party loyalty data. |
| **Consumer Journey Analytics** | Mapping multi-channel consumer journeys for precise marketing. | Zero-party, first-party website interaction data, loyalty program data. |
| **SKU Rationalization Insights** | AI-powered recommendation on SKU optimization. | Sales data, supply chain forecasts, consumer preferences, retailer inventories. |
| **Shelf & Store Execution Audits (Computer Vision)** | Automated retail compliance and shelf performance audits. | Store camera/CCTV data, shelf images, POS data. |
| **Personalized Marketing Recommendation Engine** | Hyper-personalized recommendations for targeting customers with the right product/message. | Zero-party data, first-party loyalty data, online behavior. |
| **Competitor Intelligence & Benchmarking** | Real-time monitoring of competitors’ products, pricing, and strategies. | Web scraping, retail partner data, social media analytics. |
| **Product Feature Sentiment Mining** | Identification of key features consumers love or dislike. | E-commerce reviews, social media, NLP extraction. |
| **Sustainability Sentiment Tracker** | Evaluating consumer perception of sustainability efforts. | Social listening, web forums, news articles, consumer surveys. |
| **Demand Forecasting Enhanced by AI** | Improved forecasting accuracy using diverse real-time data sources. | POS data, social signals, macroeconomic indicators, weather/location data. |
| **Retail Media Network Effectiveness Scorecard** | Cross-platform effectiveness comparison of RMNs. | Retailer-provided RMN data, incremental sales attribution models. |
| **Synthetic Consumer Panel** | Generating artificial customer panels to test product hypotheses without privacy risks. | Synthetic data, generative AI, historical transaction datasets. |
| **Localized Assortment Optimization** | AI-driven recommendations for regional/local product assortment. | Sales data, social/geographical analytics, loyalty data, retailer demographics. |
| **Brand Equity Monitor (Real-time)** | Continuous monitoring of brand health and customer perception. | Social listening, web sentiment, survey data, image/video analysis. |
| **Zero-Party Data-driven Product Innovation** | Using directly volunteered customer insights for targeted product innovation. | Zero-party data (quizzes, feedback forms), first-party loyalty insights. |
| **Retail Foot Traffic and Conversion Analysis** | Insight into shopper patterns and conversions at retail stores. | IoT sensors, camera feeds, in-store Wi-Fi tracking. |
| **Influencer and Community Impact Tracker** | Evaluating the true impact and ROI of influencer marketing. | Social network analysis, influencer follower data, campaign analytics. |
| **Consumer Loyalty and Churn Prediction** | Predictive analytics to forecast customer churn and boost retention. | CRM, transaction history, engagement metrics, AI-driven predictive modeling. |
| **Dynamic Content Generation & Testing (GenAI)** | Rapid generation and testing of marketing messaging and creative assets. | Generative AI, performance metrics, zero-party user feedback. |
| **Supply Chain-Consumer Signal Integration** | Integrating consumer sentiment and retail demand signals directly into supply chain planning. | Social signals, POS, inventory data, external market factors (weather, news). |
| **Shopper Path-to-Purchase Analytics** | Detailed insights into consumer decision-making at retail channels. | Shopper loyalty programs, POS, RFID tracking, mobile app engagement data. |
| **Retailer Collaboration Platform (Delta Sharing)** | Real-time data collaboration with retail partners for joint planning and insights. | POS data, retail promotional calendars, shared customer insight datasets. |

These use cases are relevant across different groups within Consumer Goods, but anchor primarily with Marketing.
